<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Subtropics</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
</div>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="hatnote" role="note">For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Subtropical_(disambiguation)" title="Subtropical (disambiguation)">Subtropical (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:World_map_indicating_tropics_and_subtropics.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1117" data-file-width="2000" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/World_map_indicating_tropics_and_subtropics.png/250px-World_map_indicating_tropics_and_subtropics.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/World_map_indicating_tropics_and_subtropics.png/375px-World_map_indicating_tropics_and_subtropics.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/World_map_indicating_tropics_and_subtropics.png/500px-World_map_indicating_tropics_and_subtropics.png 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:World_map_indicating_tropics_and_subtropics.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The subtropics and tropics</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Subtropical.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="628" data-file-width="1357" height="116" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Subtropical.png/250px-Subtropical.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Subtropical.png/375px-Subtropical.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Subtropical.png/500px-Subtropical.png 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Subtropical.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Areas of the world with subtropical climates</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <b>subtropics</b> are <a href="/wiki/Geographical_zone" title="Geographical zone">geographic</a> and <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="KÃ¶ppen climate classification">climate zones</a> located roughly between the tropic circle of latitude at 23.5 latitude (the <a href="/wiki/Tropic_of_Cancer" title="Tropic of Cancer">Tropic of Cancer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tropic_of_Capricorn" title="Tropic of Capricorn">Tropic of Capricorn</a>) and temperate latitudes (normally temperate latitudes refer to locations higher than 40 latitude).</p>
<p>Subtropical climates are often characterized by warm to hot summers and cool to mild winters with infrequent frost. Most subtropical climates fall into two basic types: 1- Humid Subtropical, where rainfall is often concentrated in the warmest months (for example <a href="/wiki/Brisbane" title="Brisbane">Brisbane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> or <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville,_Florida" title="Jacksonville, Florida">Jacksonville, Florida</a>) and 2- Dry summer (or Mediterranean) where seasonal rainfall is concentrated in the cooler months (for example <a href="/wiki/Naples" title="Naples">Naples</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Los_Angeles,_California" title="Los Angeles, California">Los Angeles, California</a>).</p>
<p>Subtropical climates can occur at high elevations within the <a href="/wiki/Tropics" title="Tropics">tropics</a>, such as in the southern end of the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Plateau" title="Mexican Plateau">Mexican Plateau</a> and in <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>. Six climate classifications use the term to help define the various <a href="/wiki/Temperature" title="Temperature">temperature</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">precipitation</a> regimes for the planet <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">Earth</a>.</p>
<p>A great portion of the world's deserts are located within the subtropics, due to the development of the <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_ridge" title="Subtropical ridge">subtropical ridge</a>. Within <a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">savanna</a> regimes in the subtropics, a <a href="/wiki/Wet_season" title="Wet season">wet season</a> is seen annually during the summer, which is when most of the yearly rainfall falls. Within <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean climate</a> regimes, the wet season occurs during the winter. Areas bordering warm oceans are prone to locally heavy rainfall from <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">tropical cyclones</a>, which can contribute a significant percentage of the annual rainfall. Plants such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palm_(plant)" title="Palm (plant)">palms</a>, <a href="/wiki/Citrus" title="Citrus">citrus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mango" title="Mango">mango</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lychee" title="Lychee">lychee</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Avocado" title="Avocado">avocado</a> are grown within the subtropics.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Definition">Definition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Subtropics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Definition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_locations_with_a_subtropical_climate" title="List of locations with a subtropical climate">List of locations with a subtropical climate</a></div>
<p>The tropics have been historically defined as lying between the Tropic of Cancer and Tropic of Capricorn, located at 23.45Â° north and south latitude respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> The poleward fringe of the subtropics is located at approximately 40Â° north and south latitude respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> Northern fringes of the type can go further north due to moderating effects of ocean streams, like in parts of <a href="/wiki/Southern_Europe" title="Southern Europe">Southern Europe</a> due to heat transported by the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Stream" title="Gulf Stream">Gulf Stream</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Temperatures">Temperatures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Subtropics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Temperatures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Libya_4985_Tadrart_Acacus_Luca_Galuzzi_2007.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1333" data-file-width="2000" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Libya_4985_Tadrart_Acacus_Luca_Galuzzi_2007.jpg/220px-Libya_4985_Tadrart_Acacus_Luca_Galuzzi_2007.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Libya_4985_Tadrart_Acacus_Luca_Galuzzi_2007.jpg/330px-Libya_4985_Tadrart_Acacus_Luca_Galuzzi_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Libya_4985_Tadrart_Acacus_Luca_Galuzzi_2007.jpg/440px-Libya_4985_Tadrart_Acacus_Luca_Galuzzi_2007.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Libya_4985_Tadrart_Acacus_Luca_Galuzzi_2007.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Tadrart_Acacus" title="Tadrart Acacus">Tadrart Acacus</a> desert, part of the Sahara, in western <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Several methods have been used to define the subtropical climate. In the <a href="/wiki/Trewartha_climate_classification" title="Trewartha climate classification">Trewartha climate classification</a>, a subtropical region should have at least eight months with a mean temperature greater than 10Â Â°C (50.0Â Â°F) and at least one month with a mean temperature under 18Â Â°C (64.4Â Â°F).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> German climatologists Carl Troll and Karlheinz Paffen defined Warm temperate zones as plain and hilly lands having an average temperature of the coldest month between 2Â Â°C (35.6Â Â°F) and 13Â Â°C (55.4Â Â°F) in the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Hemisphere" title="Northern Hemisphere">Northern Hemisphere</a> and between 6Â Â°C (42.8Â Â°F) and 13Â Â°C (55.4Â Â°F) in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere" title="Southern Hemisphere">Southern Hemisphere</a>, excluding <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Continental_climate" title="Continental climate">continental climates</a>. According to the Troll-Paffen climate classification, there generally exists one large subtropical zone named the warm-temperate subtropical zone,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> which is subdivided into seven smaller areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the E. Neef climate classification, the subtropical zone is divided into two parts: <i>Rainy winters of the west sides</i> and <i>Eastern subtropical climate</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> According to the Wilhelm Lauer &amp; Peter Frankenberg climate classification, the subtropical zone is divided into three parts: high-continental, continental, and maritime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> According to the Siegmund/Frankenberg climate classification, subtropical is one of six climate zones in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rainfall">Rainfall</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Subtropics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Rainfall">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Earth_rainfall_climatology" title="Earth rainfall climatology">Earth rainfall climatology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_ridge" title="Subtropical ridge">Subtropical ridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">Tropical cyclone</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wet_season" title="Wet season">Wet season</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Earth_Global_Circulation.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="477" data-file-width="556" height="257" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Earth_Global_Circulation.jpg/300px-Earth_Global_Circulation.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Earth_Global_Circulation.jpg/450px-Earth_Global_Circulation.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6d/Earth_Global_Circulation.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Earth_Global_Circulation.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hadley cells located on the Earth's atmospheric circulation.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Heating of the earth near the equator leads to large amounts of upward motion and convection along the <a href="/wiki/Monsoon_trough" title="Monsoon trough">monsoon trough</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intertropical_convergence_zone" title="Intertropical convergence zone">Intertropical convergence zone</a>. The upper-level divergence over the near-equatorial trough leads to air rising and moving away from the equator aloft. As the air moves towards the Mid-Latitudes, it cools and sinks, which leads to subsidence near the <a class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" href="/wiki/30th_parallel_(disambiguation)" title="30th parallel (disambiguation)">30th parallel</a> of both hemispheres. This circulation is known as the <a href="/wiki/Hadley_cell" title="Hadley cell">Hadley cell</a> and leads to the formation of the subtropical ridge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> Many of the world's deserts are caused by these climatological <a href="/wiki/High-pressure_area" title="High-pressure area">high-pressure areas</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> located within the subtropics. This regime is known as an arid subtropical climate, which is generally located in areas adjacent to powerful cold ocean currents. Examples of this climate, the coastal areas of southern Africa (Namibia, South Africa), south of the Canary Islands and the coasts of Peru and Chile.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britannica.com_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>The humid or monsoon subtropical climate is often located on the western side of the subtropical High. Here, unstable tropical airmasses in summer bring convective overturning and frequent tropical downpours in the hot season. In the winter (dry season) the monsoon retreats, and the drier Trade Winds bring more stable airmass and often dry weather. Areas that have this type of subtropical climate include Australia, Southeast Asia, parts of South America, and the deep south of the United States. .<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAVWOOD_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-SAVWOOD-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Monsoon regions with a wet season include western <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> the Desert Southwest of the United States,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JHorel_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-JHorel-16">[16]</a></sup> Within the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean climate</a> regime, the west coast of the United States and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mediterranean" title="Mediterranean">Mediterranean</a> coastline of Italy, Greece,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> and Turkey experience a wet season in the winter months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Similarly, the wet season in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Negev_desert" title="Negev desert">Negev desert</a> of <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> extends from October through May.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> At the boundary between the Mediterranean and monsoon climates in <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a> lies the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sonoran_desert" title="Sonoran desert">Sonoran desert</a>, which receives the two rainy seasons associated with each climate regime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>In areas bounded by warm ocean, tropical cyclones can contribute significantly to local rainfall within the subtropics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> receives over half of its rainfall from typhoons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Whipple_54_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Whipple_54-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Flora">Flora</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Subtropics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Flora">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Parque_Tingui_Curitiba_Brasil.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="510" data-file-width="768" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Parque_Tingui_Curitiba_Brasil.jpg/220px-Parque_Tingui_Curitiba_Brasil.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Parque_Tingui_Curitiba_Brasil.jpg/330px-Parque_Tingui_Curitiba_Brasil.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Parque_Tingui_Curitiba_Brasil.jpg/440px-Parque_Tingui_Curitiba_Brasil.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Parque_Tingui_Curitiba_Brasil.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Curitiba" title="Curitiba">Curitiba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>: <a href="/wiki/Live_oak" title="Live oak">Live oak</a> with <a href="/wiki/Araucaria" title="Araucaria">araucarias</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>These climates do not routinely see hard frosts or snow, which allows plants such as palms and citrus to flourish.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> As one moves toward the tropical side the slight winter cool season disappears, while at the poleward threshold of the subtropics the winters become cooler. Some crops which have been traditionally farmed in tropical climates, such as mango, litchi, and avocado, are cultivated in the subtropics. Pest control of the crops is less difficult than within the tropics, due to the cooler winters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>Tree ferns (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pteridophytes" title="Pteridophytes">pteridophytes</a>) are grown within subtropical areas, primarily within the subtropics and within topography within the <a href="/wiki/Tropics" title="Tropics">tropics</a>. <a href="/wiki/Dracaena_(plant)" title="Dracaena (plant)">Dracaena</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yucca" title="Yucca">yucca</a> can grow within the subtropics. Trees within the <a href="/wiki/Taxaceae" title="Taxaceae">Taxaceae</a> family grow within subtropical climate regimes. Apple, pear pomegranate grows well <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Varieties">Varieties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Subtropics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Varieties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Humid_variation">Humid variation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Subtropics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Humid variation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wetland_Hong_Kong.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Wetland_Hong_Kong.jpg/220px-Wetland_Hong_Kong.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Wetland_Hong_Kong.jpg/330px-Wetland_Hong_Kong.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Wetland_Hong_Kong.jpg/440px-Wetland_Hong_Kong.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wetland_Hong_Kong.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Wetland Park in <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">Humid subtropical climate</a></div>
<p>The humid subtropical climate is a subtropical climate type characterized by hot, humid summers with frequent tropical downpours of short duration and warm, and frequently dry winters. In summer, the subtropical high pressure cells bring a sultry flow of tropical air with high dew points, and daily thundershowers are typical, though brief. Normally, rainfall is concentrated in the warmest months of the year. At times, the average annual precipitation may be more evenly distributed throughout the year, or a spring maximum is present. With decreasing latitude most humid subtropical climates have drier winters and wetter summers typically, such as the USA state of <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">southeast Asia</a>.</p>
<p>Humid subtropical climates lie on the lower east side of continents, roughly between <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">latitudes</a> 25Â° and 38Â° degrees away from the equator.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mediterranean_climate">Mediterranean climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Subtropics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Mediterranean climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BCN-ParcGuell-4898.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1200" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/BCN-ParcGuell-4898.jpg/220px-BCN-ParcGuell-4898.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/BCN-ParcGuell-4898.jpg/330px-BCN-ParcGuell-4898.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/BCN-ParcGuell-4898.jpg/440px-BCN-ParcGuell-4898.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BCN-ParcGuell-4898.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Park_G%C3%BCell" title="Park GÃ¼ell">Parc GÃ¼ell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean climate</a></div>
<p>The Mediterranean climate regime resembles the climate of the lands in the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Basin" title="Mediterranean Basin">Mediterranean Basin</a>, parts of coastal southwestern North America, parts of <a href="/wiki/Western_Australia" title="Western Australia">Western</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Australia" title="South Australia">South Australia</a>, in southwestern <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> and in parts of central <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>. The climate is characterized by hot dry summers and rainfall in winter,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> in areas under the constant influence of the subtropical ridge. Inland from the immediate coastlines, mediterranean climates can take on extreme temperatures. This is seen in inland <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">Andalusia</a> in <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>. In Europe, the northernmost mediterranean climates are found along the <a href="/wiki/French_Riviera" title="French Riviera">French Riviera</a>, located at 43Â° latitude. On the immediate Atlantic coastline, the mediterranean boundary goes between <a href="/wiki/Porto" title="Porto">Porto</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vigo" title="Vigo">Vigo</a> at around 41Â° latitude. Parts of southwestern Australia around Perth have a Mediterranean climate as does areas around coastal South Africa.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Semi-desert.2Fdesert_climate">Semi-desert/desert climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Subtropics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Semi-desert/desert climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SantaBarbara2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/SantaBarbara2.jpg/220px-SantaBarbara2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/SantaBarbara2.jpg/330px-SantaBarbara2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/SantaBarbara2.jpg/440px-SantaBarbara2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SantaBarbara2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mount Benacantil, <a href="/wiki/Alicante" title="Alicante">Alicante</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Desert_climate" title="Desert climate">Desert climate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">Semi-arid climate</a></div>
<p>Arid subtropical climates are characterized by an annual average temperature of 18.2Â Â°C (64.8Â Â°F), the absence of regular rainfall and high humidity. Mild climate variants are generally located in areas adjacent to powerful cold ocean currents. Examples of this climate, the coastal areas of southern Africa (Namibia, South Africa), south of the Canary Islands and the coasts of Peru and Chile. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britannica.com_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
